Governmeent Strategy in the Power Sector
2.28      The strategy of the Government has been to reduce its dependeucy
on foreign sources for the supply of electrical energy, -which it regards as
being vital to the economy and the security of Burundi.  Thus it has given
top priGrity to the development of the Rwegura hydroelectric project which
in IDA's opinion was not the least cost solution, when the electricity
needs are considered on a regional basis.   However, it later recogLized
the advantages of the development of Ruzizi II and joined in its
construction in order to meet an anticipated growth in demand. With the
construction of both of these hydroelectric projects, Burundi is expected



- 21 -
to have an oversupply of electric power from the interconnected system
until end 1993 (para. 2.19). Therefore, the Government recognizes that the
next major task to be addressed would be the supply of electric power to
potential new consumers by extending the existing grid. Part of the funds
provided under the proposed project would be used to help achieve this
objective by the construction of 30 kV lines to supply the small towns
around the Bujumbura area.
IDA Strategy in the Power Sector
2.29      The Association's objectives in the power sector are:
(a)   to help create a soand and efficient power supply organization
through training and substantial upgrading of its managerial,
financial and technical performance;
(b)   to  support  the  least-cost expansion  of  electric  generating
capacity and the supply of electricity to unserved areas of the
country in order to foster greater economic development and
growth, to improve the quality of life and to keep down costs of
energy to householders; and
Cc)   to assure sound financial and economic policies in the power
sector including tariff structure and levels.
Objective (b) includes the sub-objective of fostering future cooperation of
the Governments to develop additional regional projects if they represent
the least-cost development options.
IDA's Participation in the Power Sector
2.30       In support of these objectives, in 1983 IDA participated in the
financing of the regional Ruzizi II Hydroelectric Project (Credits 1419-BU,
1420-Rw, 1421-ZR). The proposed project would be the second credit for the
power sector of Burundi. It is a complement to the first, and would allow
the Burundian share of the power from Ruzizi II to be available to
Burundian consumers. It would also improve the sector performance in terms
of quality and reliability of supply, and expand the existing distribution
network.    The project would  also  support  staff  training needs,  and
fiuancial and management capabilities. Funds for complementary works for
the rehabilitation and expansion of the Rwandan electricity network were
approved in June 1984 (CR 1495-RW), and Zaire has requested funds for
similar work in the Kivu province of Zaire; the latter project was
appraised in November 1984.
III. THE BORROWER AND THE IMPLEMENTING AGENCY
The Borrower
3.01       The Borrower would be the Government of the Republic of Burundi
who would relend US$12.0 million equivalent to REGIDESO, the power project
implementing agency, on terms detailed in para. 5.05.   USS0.15 million



- 22 -
would be provided to DUB through the MPWEM, for the follow up in 1987 and
1988 of the dissemination program of cooking stoves (para. 4.15), and
US$0.15 million to MPWEM for the services of a petroleum adviser
(para. 4.16).
REGIDESO
3.02       REGIDESO is a Government-owned enterprise created and organized
by the Decree 1/196 dated October 2, 1968. The objective of REGIDESO is to
generate,  transmit  and  distribute  electricity;  to  pump,  treat  and
distribute water; and to execute or supervise studies and works for new
electricity and water facilities. These duties are being carried out in a
satisfactory manner, limited to some extent by a scarcity of foreign funds
for maintenance expenses and scarcity of trained operators and qualified
management.   Therefore REGIDESO needs technical assistance in management
and training, which the proposed project addresses (paras. 4.12 and 4.14).
According to the Decree, its electricity and water tariffs would be
periodically adjusted to obtain a 'reasonable' rate of return on the net
revalued assets in operation. REGIDESO has a monopoly on the distribution
of electricity throughout the country and supply of water in urban centers,
but in fact it only operates in the urban centres of Bujumbura, Gitega,
Iuramvya and Bururi for electricity and in Bujumbura and 25 secondary
centers for water.   The electricity and water operations were organized
jointly  originally,  because  of  the  scarcity  of  qualified  management
personnel.   Now that the organization has grown,  the advisability of
separating electricity and water operations might be raised.   However,
strengthening of the existing organization has been considered to be the
first priority and management assistance has been included as a component
of the project. Electricity and water accounts and operations are already
separated and distinct, and the possibility of a formal division with a
joint administrative department would be the subject of discussion with
REGIDESO and management consultants upon completion of the management study
(para. 3.05). REGIDESO will also be the executing agency of a water supply
sector institutional and water tariffs study which is scheduled to begin
before mid 1985 with financing provided under an existing loan from the
African Development Fund (Bujumbura Water Supply Project - Phase 11). This
study is intended to clarify the respective responsabilities in the water
supply sector of REGIDESO and DHER, the latter being also responsible for
water supply in rural areas. Management assistance to be provided within
the proposed project would closely coordinate with the consultants carrying
out the water supply sector institutional and tariff study.
3.03        REGIDESO operates under the supervision of MPWEM through a six
member Board of Directors.   The Director-General of Energy, a statutory
member of the Board,  is appointed chairman by MPWEM.   Other statutory
members are the Directors-General of the Ministries of Public Health,
Planning, and the Director of Taxation. One of the two remaining members
is appointed by the Chamber of Commerce to represent high-volume industrial
consumers and, the other by the Municipality of Bujumbura to represent
small consumers. These latter appointments require the approval of MPWEM.
The Board is responsible for all decisions necessary and useful to the
accomplishment of REGIDESO's objectives, and it is solely empowered to make
decisions   regarding   REGIDESO's   assets;   to   establish   REGIDESO's
administrative and financial rules; to regulate personnel organization; to



- 23 -
propose tariff changes to Government through the MPWEM; and to prepare the
annual budget.   The Board has carried out these responsibilities  in a
reasonably satisfactory manner without excessive Government interference.
However, major investment decisions are made by the MPWEM.   The General
Manager, who is responsible for REGIDESO's day-to-day operations, is
appointed by the President of the Republic on the recommendation of the
Minister of MPWEM and the approval of the Board of Directors. Two account
controllers (Commissaires aux comptes) are appointed by the Minister of
Finance with wide powers to verify the company accounts, and to check the
accounting  systems  and  procedures.    They  submit  a yearly  report  of
verification to the Ministry of Finance and to MPWEM.
3.04          REGIDESO's organization chart is shown in Annex 11.   Two
managers, who are also appointed by the President of the Republic according
to the same procedure as for the General Manager, report to the General
Manager.   The present General Manager was appointed to his position in
March 1985. Previously, he was the Technical Manager for eleven years, in
which capacity he has proved to be competent and efficient. The Technical
Manager supervises the electricity, water, garage, and maintenance
divisions.   The electricity department is sub-divided into five units:
project studies and planning, generation, transmission and distribution,
construction, and Bujumbura operations.  The Administrative and Financial
Manager supervises four units:   personnel,  accounting, purchasing,  and
billing and  collection.   Both  managers, including  the new  Technical
Manager, are competent and efficient. In general, the responsibilities of
the senior staff members are carried out in a satisfactory manner but their
support  staff  lack  appropriate  skill,   particularly  in  marketing,
accounting, budgeting and forecasting.
Management and Personnel
3.05          REGIDESO employs a total staff of 636 which is about average
for its size as an electricity and water utility in Africa. As shown in
Annex 12, there are 39 cadres (managers and university graduates), or 6
percent of the total staff, and 597 skilled and unskilled workers. Staff
is allocated as follows: 345 for electricity, 186 for water, 105 for
administration.  Between 1979 and 1981, the number of REGIDESO staff rose
by 37% while the number of consumers rose 14%.  The ratio of consumers to
staff is now 18. 7/ One of the tasks of the management assistance team
would be to improve this ratio (para. 4.12).  Future increases of skilled
and unskilled workers should be monitored carefully to be kept within the
limits of the increase in customer base as the present ratio appears low.
The management is generally weak because of a general lack of trained
personnel both administrative and   technical, and a component of this
project would address tnis important inadequacy (para. 4.14).  Currently
four expatriates, funded by the Federal Republic of Germany, work for the
electricity and water divisions; two senior advisors and two technicians.
Furthermore, in July 1984 REGIDESO retained the services of P.A. Conseil of
France, to carry out a management diagnosis and define methods to improve
accounting and financial procedures, using funds   provided by PPF P245
7/ Botswana 9, Malawi 12, Zaire 21, Swaziland 23, Sudan 24, Madgascar 38,
Kenya 40, Ethiopia 60, Mauritius 74.



- 24 -
(para. 4.01).   The draft report was completed in March 1985; follow-up
action is recommended as in paras. 4.12 and 5.08.
Accounting and Audit
3.06      REGIDESO's accounting department is under the supervision of the
Administrative and Financial Manager. It is obliged by statute to produce
separate financial statements for its branches in the country.   The 1983
balance sheets, income statements, funds flow statements, and value added
statements were issued in April 1984, in the the Government's standard
accounts format.
3.07          Aware of weaknesses in its accounting operations, REGIDESO
requested IDA in 1979 to provide it with funds for consultants in
accounting and auditing.   REGIDESO received for this purpose US$100,000
under Technical Assistance Credit 917-BU, which was later increased to
US$125,000. In May 1981 the Ministry of Planning and REGIDESO entered into
a contract with Touche Ross of U.K. to review the accounting procedures and
revalue assets. The August 1981 report contained separate accounts for the
electricity and water departments, and a revaluation of the fixed assets
held by REGIDESO at the end of 1980.   Touche Ross also carried out a
revaluation of the 1981 assets.   In July 1984, REGIDESO entered into a
contract with Treuarbeit, of Frankfurt Germany, to audit the 1982 accounts;
the interim report was completed in October 1984.   However, because of
shortage of funds, REGIDESO did not contract the auditing of the 1983
accounts.   This exercise is being financed from funds made available
through the extension of the PPF P245 (para. 4.03).  During negotiations
agreement was reached with REGIDESO to complete the 1983 audit, and
thereafter to have its accounts audited annually by an independent auditor
acceptable to IDA, and to submit to IDA the audited financial statements
and auditor's report as soon as available but beginning with 1986 no later
than six months after the end of the fiscal year.
3.08        During negotiations it was agreed that REGIDESO would maintain
separate accounts for its electricity and water operations and would
incorporate therein an annual revaluation of its fixed assets in
operation.
3.09           Budgeting is dealt with by an assistant to the Chief of
Accounting and by a unit reporting to the Chief of Purchasing. Clear lines
of responsibility are lacking and the mission found it necessary to develop
organization charts based on discussions with the various division chiefs.
These organizational weaknesses will be reviewed and remedial action
incorporated within the management assistance program prescribed in
para. 4.12.
Data Processing
3.10             Several departments  (purchasing,  billing and collection
accounting and personnel) rely on a centralized electronic data processing
(EDP) facility of the Government.   Because none of these departments has
personnel familiar with EDP systems, the potential of such systems has not
yet been realized. The need for training in this area was noted by each of
these departments and one of the tasks of the management team (para. 4.12)



- 25 -
and training (para. 4.14) would be to ensure the efficient use of this
management tool. If, during supervision, training on this matter is found
to  proceed  satisfactorily,   REGIDESO  will  seek  financing  for  a
micro-computer.
Insurance
3.11       An earlier mission in May 1981 found that REGIDESO's assets were
not insured through commercial organizations against the usual risks of
fire, explosion, third party, etc. This inadequacy has now been corrected
and all REGIDESO assets are commercially insured through the Soci&tE
d'Assurance du Burundi.
IV. THE PROJECT
Preparation of the Project
4.01       Following the approval of the Ruzizi II Project, and with the
prospect of a significant increase in the amount of electrical power
available to Burundi (paras. 2.09 and 2.10), the Government proceeded with
the next obvious step, i.e. study of a least-cost solution to bring the
power from Ruzizi II to the center of demand in Bujumbura, and to extend
the availability of electricity service to unserved markets.  As a result,
IDA received and subsequently approved on March 28, 1983 a request from the
Government for a PPF (No. P245) in the amount of US$400.000 to carry out
the following studies in preparation for the proposed project:
(a)   feasibility of a transmission line connecting the Ruzizi II
hydro plant to the Burundian network;
(b)   feasibility of supplying with electricity the provincial
cities of Cibitoke, Rugombo, Mparambo, Bubanza, Mpanda,
Muzinda, and Katumba;
(c)   feasibility of extension of the distribution network of
Bujumbura  to   six   low-income   districts   where   urban
infrastructure was developed through IDA Urban Development
Project and an UNDP project;
(d)   a new tariff structure for REGIDESO; and
Ce)   management  consultant's  services  to  REGIDESO  to  define
methods to improve REGIDESO's management practices.
4.02      REGIDESO retained the services of Electricite de France (EdF) who
have completed their reports on the first four items covering the expansion
of the transmission and distribution networks.   P.A. Conseil (France),
consultants for the fifth item, began their services in July 1984, and
their draft report on management was completed in March 1985.
4.03      On the basis of the foregoing, t'.e Government requested that IDA
provide part of the funds needed to expand the transmission and



- 26 -
distribution facilities.   As a result, a mission visited Burundi in the
later part of June and early July 1984, to appraise the proposed project.
During appraisal, additional components, were added to the project.   In
addition, in order to expedite the project, the Government requested that
the PPF advance be raised to US$900,000 so that it could retain consultants
for the design, call for, and analysis of tenders for the power project.
Objectives
4.04        The main objective of the proposed project is to augment and
improve the reliability of supply of electricity to Bujumbura and it.
environs, by providing transmission and distribution facilities to receive
an additional source of power (Ruzizi II), to serve additional consumers,
with aview towards sustaining and improving the economic growth of the
industrial, commercial and domestic sectors of the country.  Extension of
the distribution network to low income districts of Bujumbura would
substitute electricity for kerosene for lighting, thus contributing to the
reduction of the petroleum import bill while improving the lives of those
people  served.      Extension  of  the  subtransmission  and  distribution
facilities to the seven regional towns in the north west of the capital,
would in addition to substituting electricity for kerosene for lighting,
also substitute hydro-based electricity to diesel generation in the small
private diesel plants which are operated in the coffee drying factory,
farms and missions. In addition, the provision of management assistance to
REGIDESO, establishment of a training center and the training of REGIDESO
staff, would result in improved service and financial performance through
better operating, financial and maintenance practices and strengthening of
investment planning capability. Two technical assistance programs to MPWEM
would help the Government: (i) to devise strategies to obtain imported
petroleum products at least cost (para. 4.16); and (ii) to follow up in
1987 and 1988 the dissemination of improved charcoal cooking stoves and
associated energy-saving techniques (para. 4.15).
Project Description
4.05      The main features of the project are summarized as follows:
(a) Extension of the Power Transmission and Distribution System
(i)  a  110 kV  transmission  line  (83 km) from  Ruzizi  II to
Bubanza;
(ii)  construction  of  110/30  kV  substations  in  Bubanza  and
Cibitoke, two 30 kV subtransmission lines (42 kn) to supply
the regional towns of Rugombo, Mparambo, Mpanda and Muzinda,
a 15 or 30 kV feeder to Katumba and distribution networks in
these towns;
(iii)  construction of distribution networks to consumers in six
low-income   districts   of   Bujumbura:   Bwiza,   Buyenzi,
Cibitoke 8/, Kamenge, Kinama and Musaga; and,
8/ The town of Cibitoke is situated 61 km north of Bujumbura on the road to
the Rwanda border; the Cibitoke district of Bujumbura is a new district
developed in the northeast of the capital.



- 27 -
(iv) rehabilitation of the Ruzizi I Bujumbura 70 kV line and
Bujumbura substation.
(b) Consultancy; Technical Assistance and Training to REGIDESO
(i) consulting engineering services;
(ii)  management assistance to REGIDESO; and,
(ili) construction and equipping of a training center and
technical assistance for the training of REGIDES0 staff;
(c) Technical Assistance to MPWSM
(i) follow up of the dissemination program of improved charcoal
stoves in Bujumbura (which is being carried out under the
Urban Development Project, CR 1409-BU); and,
(ii)  technical assistance to MPWEM for the services of an advisor
on petroleum matters.
Rzuzizi II/Bubanza 110 kV Transmission Line
4 06f       The single-circuit 110 kV transiission line (Map IBRD 18517)
would extend in a generally south-easterly direction from Ruzizi II
paralleling the existing 70 kV line until about the Kagunzi River, where it
would turn eastward to Bubanza.  Studies, funded by PPF P245, showed this
as the least-cost solution. Two other solutions were considered, but were
rejected because of cost: a transmission line direct to Bujumbura and a
transmission line to Rwegura, with the power transmitted from Rwegura over
the  110 kV  line now under  construction.   A fourth alternative,  the
upgrading of the existing 70 kV line to 110 kV, was studied, but this was
found to be impracticable because Bujumbura could not accept the long
shut-down needed to improve this line.   In the proposed alternative, a
single line carries power from both Rwegura and Ruzizi II, from Bubanza to
Bujumbura.   This was considered to be acceptable because the expected
outages would deprive the city of electricity for only a few hours each
year and a second line would be constructed when justified by the increase
in demand.  Bubanza, located 40 km north of Bujumbura, is well placed to
become a major dispatching point for the future development of the Burundi
transmission network. The caprscity of the transmission line would be about
40 MW, sufficient to supply the interconnected system in the event of
failure of the Rwegura Bubanza line.    The aluminum conductors with a
cross-section of 181 mm2 would be carried on galvanized steel towers, which
would also support a ground wire (94.1 mm2 of cross-section) for lightning
protection.   The line would cross Zairian and Rwandan territory, and a
condition of effectiveness is evidence satisfactory to the IDA, that REwanda
and Zaire would provide the right-of-way for the line, and would allow free
access to REGIDESO for all materials, equipment, and personnel necessary
for the construction, and continued operation and maintenance of the
transmission line outside of Burundian territory.  No problem is expected
in discussions with Rwandan and Zairian Governments because of the
precedent of the present 70 kV transmission line linking Mururu (Ruzizi I)
and Bujumbura and because Ruzizi II is being built w'-th the understanding



- 28 -
that the facility will be connected with the networks of the three
countries involved.
Cibitoke and Bubanza Substations
4.07        Additional switching and control equipment would be provided
under the proposed project at Ruzizi II to permit power to be transmitted
directly to Burundi. An intermediate substation at Cibitoke would contain
a 110/30 kV transformer (5 MVA) with the necessary switching and protective
equipment with provision for a 30 kV line towards Mparambo and Rugombo in
the north.  The major switching station at Bubanza would provide for the
incoming 110 kV lines from Rwegura and Ruzizi II and one outgoing line to
Bujumbura.   Space would be provided for a second line to Bujumbura, for
extension of 110 kV to Matongo (a potential mining center), and to Gitega,
at some time in the future. Two 110/30 kV transformers (each 5 NVA) would
be provided, one for local supply and the other as a stand-by.   The
rehabilitation needs of the Razizi I Bujumbura 70 kV line and the Bujumbura
substation (US$0.3 million; para. 2.07) would also be financed from the
proposed project. The substation and the 70 kV line connecting Ruzizi I to
Bujumbura are presently owned and operated by tha Zairian national
electricity company S.N.EL..   S.N.EL. and REGIDESO have discussed the
transfer of rights for the line and substation to REGIDESO which has the
greater interest in their effective operatikon and maintenance. A condition
of disbursement for this component would therefore be that REGIDESO has
obtained legal rights for the substation and line adequate to protect the
interests of Burundi and   A.
30 kV Subtransmission Lines
4.08      The 30 kV subtransaission lines, single circuits on wood poles,
would supply Rugumbo and Mparambo from Cibitoke (21 km), and Mpanda and
Mhuzinda from Bubanza (21 km).   IDA reviewed and is satisfied with the
designs proposed by the consultants for the transmission lines and
substations.
Distribution Extensions
4.09          The feasibility of extending electrical services into six
low-income  districts  in  Bujuabura, Cibitoke, Kinaia, Kamenge, Musaga,
Bwiza and Buyenzi (Map IBRD 18516) was studied by EdF. In 1983, the total
population of these districts was 127,000. About 13,600 a of 10 kV, and
106,430 a of 400 kV distribution lines, and 30 transformers of various
cspacit!es (50 kVA to 630 kVA) totalling a capacity of 7,550 kVA would be
installed to connect 3,300 new consumers in 1986 and 1987.   Details are
given in Annex 13.  The infrastructure work in the district of Musaga was
constructed with funds of an UNDP project; those of the other five
districts  were   financed  from  the  IDA  Urban  Development  Project
(CR  1049-BU).   The urban infrastructure provided within IDA and UNDP
credits included street improvements, drainage canals, additional water
distribution standpipes and construction of public lighting and electricity
networks along main streets. Interest from households for electrification
in the Kamenge, Bwiza and Buyenzi has been relatively high although no
special effort was made by REGIDESO to promote house electrification at
that early stage. There were 724 consumers in June 1984 and this



- 29 -
represented about 4% of the estimated number of households in these
districts.   The consultants evaluated the potential demand taking into
account past trends, analysis of expected number of connections with
respect to household incomes and actions proposed by EdF to be taken by
REGIDESO to provide better terms for connection charges.  To develop the
distribution networks in the regional towns of north of Bujumbura, about
20,500 m of 400 V lines and 21 transformers of various capacities totalling
2,000 kVA would be installed to connect about 360 consumers, a few of which
will be supplied directly from the 30 kV lines, e.g. the military camps,
flour mill, tobacco drying factory, hospitals, missions, farms.   Details
are given in Annex 14.  The town of Katumba, about 15 km from Bujumbura
would be provided with electricity from Bujumbura-Uvira line, owned by
S.N.EL., by a short feeder line; the voltage of the feeder line will be
determined following review of the feasibility studies being carried out by
the Consultants to S.N.EL. within the proposed Zaire Power II Project.
Four pole mounted transformers of a total capacity of 200 kVA and about
1,000 m of 400 V distribution lines would be constructed to connect about
60 consumers. The proposed design is acceptable.
4.10        REGIDESO requires the new consumers to pay a connectlon charge
of about BuF 60,000 (US$512) which is about the cost of the connection
material and equipment, including meters. REGIDESO is reluctant to delete
meters on the grounds that, in general, consumption increases quite
rapidly.  9/   EdF estimated  that households with incomes greater  than
BuF 26,00O7month would be able and willing to finance house wiring and the
actual  connection  charges.    This  would  represent  about  29%  of  the
households  in  Bwiza and  10% in the other districts.   The number of
additional consumers is estimated to be around 1,100. The consultants also
estimated that reducing the bulk payment of connection charges to about BuF
30,000 (US$256) would lower to BuF 20,000/month the threshold at which a
household income easily affords the wiring and connection expenses,
allowing  2,200  additional  families  to  afford  these  expenses.    The
management of REGIDESO recently decided to collect the connection charges
in monthly installments over six months in Bujumbura and twelve months
outside the capital. The Development Bank of Burundi provides loans for 1
to ljyears for connection charges and house wiring; employees of the
private companies are given salary advances for such expenses.  Therefore
it is expected that in the implementation period of the proposed project
about 3,720 new consumers in total will be connected; this means about 7
connections per day, which is within the implementation capability of
REGIDESO (paras. 3.05 and 4.22). About 25% of the households would thus be
electrified by the end of the project. The actual average consumption for
the whole of Bujumbura which is about 4,157 kWh/year per c-)nnection, shows
the tendency in the past to restrict electrification to the larger
consumers.   A study for defining optimal standards for connections,  a
connection charges policy and amount of consumption to be charged at the
lifeline tariff rate is included in che proposed project.   The terms of
reference  and  the  consultants  would  be  acceptable  to  IDA.    During
negotiations agreement was reached that this study would be completed by
June 30, 1986 and that the Government and REGIDESO would implement promptly
9/ Random checks among existing consumers show that many of them consume
around 2500-5800 kWh per year; the average consumption for all Bujumbura
is about 4,157 kWh/year.



- 30 -
thereafter and following an exchange or u!ews with IDA, a new connections
policy based on the recommendations of the study. The objective of the
policy should be that, where additional connections are economically
justified, demand is not deterred by unnecessarily high capital charges
that could be spread over time through the tariffs.
Consulting Engineering Services
4.11        Consulting engineering services would cover the preparation of
bid documents, evaluation of bids and construction supervision for the
power transmission and distribution components.  The cost of engineering
services is estimated to be US$0.95 million of which US$0.8 million would
be in foreign exchange.
Management Assistance
4.12           The draft  report  of  the  study  financed under  PPF  P245
(para. 4.01) to improve management, accounting and financial planning was
completed in March 1985 and discussed during negotiations. A condition of
Credit Effectiveness would be that REGIDESO and IDA would agree on an
action program, based on the recommaendations of the management diagnosis
study,  to  strengthen  REGIDESO's  management  performance,  to  improve
administratLve and financial operations and to implement corrective
measures. The action program would be implemented with the assistance of a
management team. During negotiations agreement was reached that, REGIDESO
would retain the services of a management assistance team at the latest by
December  31,  1985.   The terms of reference and qualifications of the
personnel would  be acceptable to  IDA.   IDA has estimated  that  these
services would cost about US$1.15 million of which US$1.0 million would be
in foreign exchange. The main emphasis of this component would be in the
areas of accounting, finance, and investment planning, although other
activities such as procurement and marketing would be given appropriate
attenticn.
Studies
4.13         With the assistance of the management team, and possibly an
engineering  consultant,  a  ten-year  least-cost  development  plan  for
investments  in  the electricity    sector,  taking into account  regional
potential projects and demand would be prepared for review by IDA by June
30,  1986.   This plan, would be updated and discussed annually with IDA.
Close cooperation would be required with EGL (para. 2.04) DHER (para.
2.13),  and  the  training consultants  (para.  4.14).    Need  for  such  a
long-term development plan derives from the presence of the electrical
energy surplus (para. 2.19) which poin.s to the fact that Burundi
over-invested in generation facilities, and under-invested in transmission
and distribution. A study of the long-run marginal cost of electricity and
tariff structure is being carried out financed by PPF 245 and will be
completed in mid-1985.   An update of the study will be carried out 1"
19871198P in parallel with the tariff study to determine the level of the
tariffs for the sale of electricity by SINELAC to the three national
utilities. Funds provided under this component would also be utilised for
the distribution connections policy study (para. 4.10), a revaluation of
REGIDESO'S assets at the end of 1984, its subsequent revisions and audit of



- 31 -
Its 1984 accounts.   IDA has estimated that these studies would cost about
US$0.175 million.
Training
4.14       REGIDESO does not carry out organized training programs for its
staff. Training under the proposed project would be both for the Technical
and the Administrative and Financial Departments. The former would Include
vocational orientation and advanced vocational training for operators,
foreimu and professional staff, applicable to thelr current jobs and for
future responsibilities, with an emphasis on the introduction of new
technologles such as data processing.   The AdministratLve and Financial
Department's training would include a comprehensive orientation for newly
recrulted staff and advanced traLnitg both for current jobs and for new
responsibilities for existing staff.   During negotiations, agreement was
reached with REGIDESO that by October 1, 1985 a Training ffauager and
Burundian trainers satisfactory to IDA, would be appointed to act as
counterparts to three training consultants to be financed as part of this
project and to be appointed by the same date. The Training Manager would
report directly to the General Manager. Description of the proposed action
plan and of the requlred qualiflcations for holders of these posts ls given
in Annex 15. One firm would supply the three tralners, the senior of whom
should have responsibllity for the design and construction of the proposed
training center (physLcal facilities), and the preparation and issue of bid
documents for the equipment, also to be financed as part of the proposed
project.   The senior consuLtant would have a broad knowledge  of  the
organization of training activities in a power utillity, including
on-the-job and in-center training with speclfic reference to the operation
and maintenance of hydroelectrlc facilities, the second would have training
expertise in construction, operations and maintenance of transuission and
distribution systems, while the tbird would be competent in teaching
current utility financial and accounting practices. The terms of reference
and the qualifications of the consultants, which were discussed during
negotiations and which will be further discussed with GTZ (Annex 15), would
be subject to IDA's approval.   With an allowance of .oout US$0.3 million
for equipment and facilities, the total cost of this component is estimated
to  be  US$1.5  million.    Agreement  was  reached  with  REGIDESO  during
negotiations:
(a) that the training consultants and their counterparts would
prepare a detailed plan, acceptable  to IDA. for training of
technical, financial and administrative personnel and manpower
projections for the next five years; and,
(b) to initiate a training program by September 1, 1986.
Follow-up of DisseminatLon Program of I!proved Charcoal Stoves in Bujumbura
4.15          This component would be a continuation of the current stove
dissemination program which is part of IDA's Urban Development Project
(CR 1049-BU), and would be carried out by DUB, the project unit which has
been responsible for the work to date. The closing date of Credit 1049-WU
is presently December 31, 1985; but it is expected that the date will be
extended by at least one year, to December 31, 1986.  The funds of the



- 32 -
proposed project would be used to sustain the dissemination program in 1987
and 1988. The technical objective of the stove program has been achieved;
with assistance to modify the design by an ESMAP mission, the Urban
Development Project has produced an improved stove which, at a slightly
higher production cost than a traditional stove, consumes about 30% less
charcoal. The problem now is one of how to market this modified stove. A
marketing rather than educationally-oriented. promotion campaign is being
set up within the Urban Development Project, aiming at the training of
artisans in production of the new stove, and of about 20 "animatrices' in
methods of disseminating the stoves and associated energy-saving techniques
of cooking to Bujumbura householders.   This campaign would start by mid
1985 and should be sustained at least four years in order to facilitate
gradual behavior changes from traditional cooking practices.   It is also
considered essential that such a promotion program should be applied
without interruption; and therefore the proposed component would provide
for continuity when CR 1049-BU is closed.   The total base cost of the
component is estimated as US$135,000 of which US$100,000 is foreign
currency cost. It is intended that the proposed Forestry II Project, now
being appraised, would contain a provision for training in charcoal
production and close cooperation would be maintained between the Urban
Development Project and the two proposed projects.  The Government will
continue the dissemination program beyond the closing date of C% 1049-BU,
within the same institutional framework as agreed or reviewed within the
Urban Development Project and it will submit a separate completion report
when the program is terminated in end-1988.
Technical Assistance to the MPWEM
4.16         This component of the project would cover the services of an
adviser to MPEWN who would assist in devising strategies which may be
employed to obtain imported petroleum products at least cost, and to
develop pricing policies for the sale of these products within Burundi and
to train two Burundian couaterparts. The mission has included an allowance
of US$100,000 to cover the cost of services, travel and subsistence of the
advisor. Services would be spread over a period of two years, with short
visits to Burundi. Travel to potential vendors and distributors would also
be required. Travel expenses in foreign currency of the adviser will also
be financed from the credit.   Agreement was reached with the Government
during negotiations that an adviser acceptable to IDA would be appointed by
December 31, 1985 and that his terms of reference, based on those prepared
by an ESMAP mission would be agreed with IDA.

Government has agreed would not be levied on the project, and excluding
interest during construction. The foreign exchange component is estimated
to be BuF 2,320 million (US$17.05 million equivalent), about 78% of the
total project cost.   The total finaicing requirement, including interest
during construction (BuF 377 million; US$2.7 million equivalent), is
estimated to be BuF 3,338 million (US$24.5 million). The estimated cost of
the principal components of the project are shown on che following page.

Basis for Estimates
4.18          The cost estimates for the consulting services, management
assistance, training, petroleum adviser and cooking stoves foLlow up
program have been prepared by IDA, (paras. 4.11-4.16) while the costs of
the other components have been estimated by RECIDESO's consultants, EdF
International. These cost estimates were reviewed by IDA and were found to
be reasonable. Physical contingencies of 10% were added to each component
to provide an allowance for unforeseen increases in the volume of work.
Price contingencies  for the project cost presented in BuF are based on
domestic inflation estimated as follows: 18% in 1985, 12% in 1986, and 10%
from 1987 onward; price contingencies for the project cost expressed in
USDollars are based on an international inflation rate as follows: 5Z in
1985, 7.5% in 1986 and 8% in 1987 and 1988. The price contingencies were
considered on the basis of the BuF exchange rate being adjusted to
compensate for the difference between domestic and international inflation.
Financing Plan
4.19       The proposed IDA credit of US$12.3 million would finance about
56% of the estimated project cost of BuF 2,961 million (US$21.8 million
equivalent) and about 72% of the estimated foreign currency expenses of the
project of BuF 2,320 million (US$17.05 million), in both cases excluding
interest during construction. It would be used to finance:
(a) repayment of the PPF (US$0.9 million) for the preliminary
engineering study and detailed design and preparation of
contract documents;
(b) 100% of the foreign cost of the engineering services,
management assistance, and studies;
(c)  90% of  the totai cost of the  110 kV  transmission line;
Bubanza and Cibitoke substations and training center; and,
(d) 100% of the foreign cost of the petroleum adviser and follow-
up of the cooking stoves dissemination program.
4.20       Colenders would finance US$7.3 million.  The Government informed
IDA that funds would be providad by the Belgian Government, CCCE of France
and Deutsche Gesellschaft fur Technische Zusammenarbeit (GTZ) of Germany.
CCE would finance the expansion of the distribution network in the low-
income districts of Bujumbura and the distribution networks in the regional
towns north of Bujumbura (para. 4.08 and 4.09).   The project has been
accepted by the common French Burundese economic commission in May 1984.
The Belgian Governament would finance the 30 kV subtransmission lines. GTZ
would finance the technical assistance part (US$0.8 million) of the
training component (para. 4.14). A condition of effectiveness of the IDA
credit would be the receipt of evidence satisfactory to IDA, that the
effectiveness conditions of the other external sources of funds have been
met.
4.21            REGIDESO  would  finance  local  currency  costs  of  about
US$2.15 million equivalent (10% of the project total cost, excluding IDC).
A summary of the detailed financing plan shown in Annex 16 is as follows:

Status of Engineering and Implementation
4.22          REGIDES0 would be responsible for the implementation of the
power transmission and distribution components of the project and would be
assisted  by engineering  consultants.    REGIDESO  signed an engineering
contract with EdF of Franc.2 (the consultants for the initial study). This
consultant is acceptable to IDA, and during negotiations, agreement was
reached that REGIDESO would continue to employ consultants satisfactory to
IDA.  The construction of the 110 kV and 30 kV transmission lines and
substations would be carried out by contractors. REGIDESO has experience
in building 30 kV, 10 kV and 400 V distribution lines and substations, and
would be competent to carry out similar work for this project. Bowever,
the volume of work would be too great, and REGIDESO intends to concentrate
its work crews on the distribution extensions, for which they are well
qualified, and call tenders for the the 30 kV lines. The preparation of
preliminary designs, and tender documents for the transmission lines are
scheduled to be completed by June 30, 1985 and construction work completed
by mid-1988 as shown on the implementation schedule (Annex 17).  Tenders
for the electrification of the peripheral districts of Bujumbura would be
issued by June 30, 1985 with a view to completion by December 31, 1987.
These schedules appear reasonable in view of the fact that the work to be
performed does not require major structures. As the contracts will include
commonly purchased material and equipment, and erection services would be
routine in nature, risks of cost overruns are estimated to be small.
Procuremnnt
4.23       The materials and equipment including erection services, to be
financed by the proposed IDA Credit would be purchased in accordance with
IDA's guidelines for international competitive bidding.   Procurement for
cofinanced items of the project would be in accordance with the funding
agency's normal practices. Services to be provided by consultants and to
be financed by IDA would be awarded according to IDA guidelines on the
appointment  of consultants.   On  the  following  page  is  a  tabulation
indicating the method of procurement of the various components.

Disbursements
4.24      The proceeds of the Credit would be disbursed over 5 years on the
basis given in para. 4.19.  The remaining funds would be disbursed from
other colenders and from LtEGIDESO.  The closing date for the Credit would
be December 31, 1989. The disbursement schedule (Annex 18) differs from
the average power project and from Burundi project profiles because IDA
would be providing funds for a limited portion (i.e. only the transmission
line and substations) of a complete power project (i.e. including
generation).    The  schedule  is  consistent with  the  transmission  and
distribution project profile for the Eastern Africa Region. A condition of
disbursement for the expenses for the rehabilitation of the Bujumbura
substation now owned by S.N.EL. (Zaire) would be that REGIDESO obtain legal
rights adequate to protect the interests of Burundi and IDA (para. 4.07).
4.25       A special account (revolving fund) of US$0.5 million, financed
under the Project, would be established in an account to be opened in the
Bank of the Republic of Burundi for the purpose of alleviating Government's
difficulty in pre-financing expenditures to be reimbursed under the IDA
Credit, and operated under terms and conditions acceptable to IDA.  The
special account would be replenished on a semi-annual basis upon receipt of
docmentary evidence to be provided by REGIDESO. Should any disbursements
be made from the special account which are not-acceptable to IDA, the



- 37 -
Government would deposit the corresponding amount into the Special
Account. Agreements on terms and conditions for using the Special Account
were reached at negotiations.

proposed detailed guidelines for a project monitoring system are given in
Annex 19.   The project is expected to be completed by June 30,  1989.
Preparation of a project completion report not later than six months after
project completion was agreed during negotiations.   Some key performance

V. FINANCIAL ANALYSIS
Present Financial Position
5.01           REGIDESO's financial performance has been constrained  by
inadequate electricity tariffs and high operating expenses for both
electricity and water.   This is evidenced by its 1983 results which show
financial rates of return on revalued assets for electricity and water
operations of 2.1% and 5.8Z, respectively, resulting in a financial rate of
return of 2.8Z for REGIDESO overall.  The operating ratios in 1983 were,
88%, 86% and 87% for electricity operations, water operations and overall
REGIDESO, respectively.   The current ratio of 2.6 reflects the excessive
level of receivables for sales of electricity and water, which were
equivalent to eleven months of billing as of December 31, 1983; reduction
of receivables through more effective billing and persistent collection is
an objective of REGIDESO (para. 5.03). The debt/equity ratio at 61:39 was
high reflecting large borrowings undertaken for expansion of generating
capacity and transmission (para.  2.09).   The financial statements  for
REGIDESO for the year 1983 are summarized in kanex 20. The principal items
are as follows:

The Decree establishing REGIDESO requires that tariffs should produce a
reasonable' rate of return on net revalued assets in operation. The 1983
returns are considered to be below a reasonable level, and could be
improved progressively primarily through more frequent tariff adjustments
and  attainment  of  cost  reflective  pricing.    For  its  water  supply
operations, revenues should be at least sufficient to cover operating
expenses and debt service and to provide a reasonable contribution to the
investment  program.   During  negotiations, agreement was reached that
REGIDESO would apply this principle and reach agreement with the Government
and IDA on an acceptable level of contribution to its investment program.
For its electricity operations, REGIDESO has agreed to take all measures
necessary including adjustment of its tariff level, to meet rates of return
on its net assets as shown in para.  5.14.   Financial projections for
electricity operations are at Annex 21 (pages 1-4) and for water supply
operations at Annex 21, page 5.

The long-term debt proportion of 61X is marginally high and should not be
allowed to increase. The policy of the Government of Burundi requires that



- 39 -
REGIDESO pay all financing charges and principal on on-lent funds without
capitalizing interest during construction. Based on its recent performance
experience, REGIDESO may have difficulty for the next two or three years in
generating adequate funds to meet its cash requirements and finance its
investment program, and may be forced to undertake short-term borrowing
from the Government or other sources to ensure coverage of all operating
and capital investment needs. REGIDESO's total indebtness should therefore
be monitored carefully.  During negotiations, it was agreed that REGIDESO
would not incur debt unless internal cash generated for the twelve months
preceding incurrence of the debt is at least 1.5 times the maximum debt
service requirements for any succeeding years.
Receivables
5.03          As of December 31,  1983, total receivables amounted to the
equivalent of 11 months billing for electricity and water.  Of the amount
outstanding, approximately 62% was due from Government and municipalities.
During 1984 these arrears have been reduced by 30% but further improvement
is  required.   During negotiations  it was agreed that the amounts of
receivables for electricity and water consumption: (i) for Government and
municipalities would be reduced to 6 months of billings by December 1986
and 4 months of billings by December 1987 and thereafter; and, (ii) for
other consumers would be reduced to 4 months of billings by December 1985
and 3 months of billings for those consumers billed on a monthly basis and
4 months of billings for consumers billed every two months by December 1986
and thereafter. Preparation of an action plan acceptable to IDA to reduce
Government's and municipalities arrears to 6 months of electricity and
water billings by December 1986, would be a condition of effectiveness.

5.07           In addition to the proposed project,  the main investment
expenditures over the period are detailed in paragraph 2.27 (Annex 10).
5.08            REGIDESO has no systematic investment planning and only
rudimentary project accounting and budgeting systems, and requires
extensive assistance to attain acceptable standards in both areas (para.
4.12). The management diagnosis financed under PPF P245,completed in March
1985, offers recommendations which will form the basis of an action program
to improve sales management, accounting and budgeting, investment planning,
marketing and procurement. The action program will be submitted to IDA as
a condition of Credit Effectiveness (para. 4.12) and its implementation
monitored during the life of the project, after approval by IDA.
Tariffs
5.09         Details of Burundi's tariff structure are given in Annex 22.
Electricity tariffs are approved by the Government on the basis of proposal
from the National Price Commission which reviews proposals by MPWEM.
Tariffs were last increased on January 1, 1985 by about 20Z, five years
after the previous increase.  Present tariffs are 10.6 BuF/kWh (US9.2/kWh)
for low voltage service and a demand charge plus energy charge combination
for medium voltage service which currently averages approximately 8.0
BuF/kWh  (US6.8/kWh).    The  1985  increase  would  be  adequate  to meet
projected operating and investment requirements and yield a rate of return
on net fixed assets of 3.8X, an improvement over 1984 performance.   The
1985 increase affected only low voltage tariffs which were increased by
42Z.  The present low voltage tariff level is only 60% of the estimated
LRMC for this voltage (BuF 18.8/kWh - US416.1/kWh) and medium voltage
ariffs are abo   65Z of the LKMC for this voltage level (BuF 12.1/kWh -
USOl. 3/kwh) (para. 6.13).  The LRMC study by EdF International, as revised
by IDA (para. 6.13), shows that the ratio of the low voltage tariffs to the
medium voltage tariffs should be about 1.5 since low voltage power has a
higher cost/kWh than medium voltage power.   Therefore, future increases
should continue to concentrate on low voltage tariffs.
5.10        In addition to cost factors, consideration should also be given
to tariff structure adjustments which will encourage extension of service
to  lower  income  groups.    These  considerations  will  include  cross-
subsidization between and within consumer categories, use of 'inverted'
block rates or 'lifeline' rate structures, and modifications of the
connection charge policy (para. 4.10).  This extension of service policy
has been discussed with REGID6SO and Government both of which suppor   he
concepto
5.11            It was agreed during  negotiations  that a new structure
consistent with the findings of the tariff study (para. 4.01) would be
implemented in 1985 and would be fully effective at the beginning of 1986
and that REGIDESO and Government would review the tariff structure
annually, noting:



- 42 -
(a) the desirability of moving towards marginal costs,
(b) the means by which electricity service can be extended to lower
income groups including
(i)   acceptable levele of cross-subsidization between categories
of consumers,
(ii)  acceptable  levels of cross-subsidization within the low
voltage domestic category by use of 'linverted' block rates
or 'lifeline' rate structures,
(iii) modification of connection charge requirements.
5.12          It was further agreed during negotiations that REGIDES0 and
Government would implement and approve annually tariffs developed in
accordance with the objectives outlined in paragraph 5.11 which in total
would produce revenues sufficient to earn agreed rates of return
(para. 5.14).

Other Fiuancial Covenants
5.14        It was agreed during negotiations with REGIDESO and Government
that tariff adjustments would be made to produce a rate of return on net
revalued assets of not less than 4.0% in 1985, 1986 and 1987; 4.5% in 1988;
6.5 in 1989 and 8.0% in 1990 and thereafter.   The lower returns in the
earlier years are reasonable as higher rates of return would require
unrealistically large tariff increases, increasing the difficulty of
expanding service to low income consumers.

(para. 4.13), major unprogrammed capital expenditures could have a
significant effect upon the future financial position of REGIDESO and could
distort least-cost development.   It was therefore agreed at negotiations
that REGIDESO would not commit itself without prior consultation with
IDA to any capital investment in excess of US$5 million and would ensure
that every investment in the electricity sector would be economically and
financially justified.
VI. PROJECT JUSTIFICATION AND RISKS
The 110 kV Transmission Line
6.01           Construction of the Ruzizi II generating station is now
underway, and Burundi is committed to provide 1/3 of the cost of the
project (para. 2.10). It has also entered into a contract with SINELAC to
purchase sufficient power to cover 1/3 of the cost of operation,
maintenance and debt service, and without the 110 kV line connecting Ruzizi
II to Burundi, Burundi could not receive power from the generating station.
Least Cost Solution
6.02       The mission has reviewed the EdF report (paras. 2.17 and 4.02)
and is in agreement with the recommendation that the least-cost method of



- 44 -
bringing electric power from the Ruzizi II generating station to Burundi,
is via a 110 kV transmission line joining the Rwegura Bujumbura line, now
under construction at Bubanza.   The selection of alternative operating
voltages would be inappropriate in the long term, and the route selected,
with termination at Bubaaza, is the least costly of the several routes
investigated. The mission also agrees that the schedule for commissioning
the line by 1988 is also justified, as costs of possible use of diesel
units and shortages are greater than those associated to building the
transmission line with the commissioning date of 1988 rather than 1989.
Regional Investment Program
6.03        Return on Investment.  The economic rate of return on a power
program is normally calculated as the discount rate at which the present
value of the capital and operating costs of the program equals the present
value of the incremental benefits, as measured by the va'ue of energy
production using existing and projected future tariffs and the assumed load
growth.   This project is an important component of a regional program
designed to provide electrical energy to the Great Lakes Region of Burundi,
Rwanda,  and Zaire.   Thus,  because  it is not possible  to compute  the
economic rate of return on only a part of a program, the economic rate of
return on the total investments for electrical energy in the Region was
computed.
6.04        The sale of energy from Rwegura and Ruzizi II is expected to
begin in l988, and for the purposes of computation of benefits, only the
demand above the capability of the existing system has been considered.
Thus, total sales from Rwegura and Ruzizi II were assumed o be 26 GWh in
1988 and would rise to 224 GWh in 1995, equivalent to the stations' maximum
capacity of 264 GWh, in accordance with the forecast demand which is
eStLmated to increase at 10% annually in the 1984-1995 period (Annex 9).
The sales were determined  by reducing  the rated output of generating
stations by 15% to cover estimated losses in the transmission and
distribution system, and revenues were computed by mltiplying the
resulting sales in Burundi, Rwanda and Zaire (Kivu) by the respective
forecast tariffs (Annex 24).
6.05        The total cost of the program was based on constant end-1984
estimates of costs for the Rwegura and Ruzizi II projects, and the
complementary works in Burundi, Rwanda, and Zaire. An allowance of US$1.0
million in 1988 and 1989, decreasing to US$0.4 million in 1994, was added
to the cost of the complementary works in each country to cover local
distribution extensions.  The cost of operation and maintenance was based
on annual charges of 1% of the capital cost of generation, and 3% and 7% of
the   capital   costs   of   transmission   and   distribution   facilities,
respectively.   The life of the project was assumed to be 30 years.   A
salvage value allowance of 40Z was included for the generation facilities
only.   Price escalation and interest during construction (IDC) were not
included in the computations.
6.06      Based on the foregoing assumptions the economic rate of return on
the regional investment program was computed to be 8%.   By taking into
account the economic benefit (consumers' surplus) deriving from the
availability of hydropower rather than high cost diesel-generated power



- 45 -
which it is estimated fifteen percent of consumers consumers would be ready
to buy, the economic rate of return was determined to be 13x.   In this
case, benefits for this portion of sales were based on alternative costs of
diesel generation.  The rates of return have been found to be comparable to
those given ia the staff appraisal report for the Razizi 11 Regional
Hydroelectric Power Project (4303 EAP; May 1982) The economic rates of
return are sensitive to changes in costs and revenues.  If the capital cost
of the project increase by 102, the rates of return on the project reduce
to 7Z and 122, respectively, excluding and including consumers' surplus.
Also, if the growth of demand for energy is 9X p.a., which results in a
delay of one year in the use of RuzzitL II and Rwegura, the rates of return
would  be  72 and  12Z,  respectively.    If  both  events  were  to  occur
simultaneously the rates of return would be 6.5X and 112, respectively.
Annex 24 contains details on the foregoing computations and assumptions.
In all cases, the economic rates of return are acceptable.
110/30 kV Substations at Bubanza and Cibitoke, 30 kV Lines to the Regional
Towns  and  Distribution  Development at  the  Regional Towns,  including
Katumba
6.07          Return on Investment.  EdF recomended the construction of
110/30 kV substations supplied from the proposed 110 kV transmission line
and 30 kV lines to supply the towns of Cibitoke and Bubanza and other small
towns in the ares (Rugombo,  4parambo, "4xinda, Mpanda).  There are small
diesel units in the farms and missions in the area and a tobacco drying
factory is being constructed in Cibitoke. The consultants concluded that
the potential loads are sufficiently large and the economic activity levels
of these towns sufficiently high to expand the units and install new ones.
Therefore the consultants determined the economic rates of return for the
Investments comparing the proposed project components with their diesel
alternatives.  IDA preferred a more conservative approach and limited the
saving in substituting dlesel-generated electricity by hydro-based
electricity only for existing diesel plants. According to IDA's estimates,
it is expected that about 1.5 GWh/year of diesel generation will be
substituted by hydro based electricity supplied from the interconnected
system.  With the actual cost of diesel oil, the annual savings of fuel
costs would amount to about BuF 48.6 (US$0.4) million. Revenues from the
forecast sales on top of the 1.5 GWh were determined using projected
tariffs. Economic analysis was carried out for three project components:
(1) Cibitoke, Rugombo and Mparambo which will be supplied from the
Cibitoke substatlon; (2) Bubanza, Mpands and Muzinda, which will be
supplied from the Bubanza substation; and (3) Katumbs, which will be
supplied from the Bujunbura-Uvirs line and where IOZ of the fore^st sales
is expected  to substitute generation from  very  small diesel units  by
individuals.  In the case of Cibitoke, the capital costs for the 30 kV
lines include the cost of the substation, while for the Bubanza case, only
a portion of the estimated substation cost was included, because the main
expenditures would be required in any event, for connecting the incoming
110 kV lines from Rwegura and Ruzizi II and the outgoing line to
Bujumbura. For Katumba, only a feeder was considered because the Bujumbura
Uvira line crosses the town. Price escalation and IDC were not included in
the computatLons. The cost of operation and maintenance was assumed to be
2% and 7X of the capital costs of the subtransmission and distribution
facilities, respectively, and the life of the projects was assumed to be 30
years.



- 46 -
6.08         The economic rate of return for each project group has b-een
computed as the discount rate at which the present value of the carital,
energy and operation and maintenance costs equal the present value of the
incremental benefits, which in theFa cases were measured by the value of
savings  by  substituting  diesel  generated  electricity  by  hydro  based
electricity and the value of sales (on top of the portion saved) using
projected tariffs (Annex 25).   Energy costs were based on thle LR!C as
determined in Annex 23.  Based on the foregoing assumptions the rates of
return would be as follows:
- Cibitoke group: 17%
- Bubanza group: 11%
- Katumba: 11%
No benefit was taken into account for the likely greater availability of
the transmission and distribution facilities versus diesel plants
(maintenance and fuel supply problems and foreign exchange need for diesel
oil).   Therefore the economic rates of return are stated conservatively.
The economic rates of return, excluding consumers' surplus were calc lated
as follows:
- Cibitoke group: 11%
- Bubanza group: 10%
- Katumba: 9Z
6.09       The economic rates of return are sensitive to the capital costs
and demand forecasts. Results are summarized as follows:
Economic Rate of Return (Z)
Cibitoke    Bubanza    Katumba
Group       Group       Group
- Capital costs increased by 10%             16          11         10
- Demand for energy is not so
great as to delay estimated
sales by one year                          15          11         10
- Both events occur                          14          10          9
The economic rates of return are acceptable.
Distribution Extensions of Low Income Districts of Bujumbura
6.10        Return on Investment.  EdF has also completed their studies on
the electrification of six low-income districts on the periphery of
Bujumbura and calculated ar economic rate of return for the whole
development. However, IDA preferred to view each district which could be
electrified as an individual project and calculated separate rates of
return as the discount rate at which the present value of he capi al,
energy and operating costs equal the present value of the incremental
benefits, (in this case measured by the value of sales) using projected
tariffs and savings from the small diesel units to be used by entrepreneurs
and savings from the kerosene wick lamps; particular attention was not paid
to double-count the benefits.  Energy costs were based on the LRMC (Annex
23); annual operation and maintenance costs were assumed to be 7Z of the



- 47 -
capital costs. Demand forecasts taken into account as the base case were
those projected by EdF  (about 2,000 kWh/annum per consumer), lO/ and
sensitivity studie3 were carried out with    00, 1,500 and 1,000 kMT/aimum
per consumer. Taking into account past trends in the already electrified
medium to low-income districts such as Ngagara and Nyakabiga, access to
electricity service stimulates commercial activity such as service
stations, garages, small workshops; therefore it is estimated that the
value of 2,000 kWh/annum per consumer is reasonable and 1,000 kWh/annum per
consumer (without Increase over the life of the project) is a conservative
minimum.  Furthermore, it is also estitbated that about 10% of the sales
would substitute for generation from small diesel units used in service
stations, garages and workshops and the total demand would be inelastic to
tariff increases within any reasonable range.  For each new consumer 100
kWh/year was assumed to be used to substitute for the kerosene wick lamps.
The value of sP2.es (ca top of the portion substituted) was determined using
tariffs (para. 5S.13). Annex 26 contains details of the computations based
on the above assumptions.
6.11       Based on the foregoing assumptions, the economic rates of return
for the base case on the distribution extensions were found to be as
follows:
Cibitoke       10%   Kamenge       15%     Bwiza        20%
Kinaia         10%   Musaga        13%     Buyenzi      14%
The economic rate-of-return for  the whole component was calculated as
14%. No benefit was ascribed to the better quality of life provided by
electric lighting; therefore, the economic rates of return are also stated
conservatively.
6.12          The rates of return are sensitive to the demand forecast
(para.  6.10).    Sensitivity  studies  were  carried  out using  different
percentages of the expected sales and a cost increase of 10%. Results are
given in Annex 26 and summarized in the following table for the whole
component:

of the project; however, the additional savings in imported diesel oil and
kerosene which are included in the tabulated ERR results shown above, are
large enough and to produce acceptable economic rates of return.
Long-Run Marginal Cost
6.13       Consultants (EdF International) determined a long run marginal
cost (LRMC) for electricity in their tariff study (para. 4.02). However,
as IDA, believes that the load forecast and the investment program
considered  in  the  study  were  too  optimistic,  the  LRMC  for  the
interconnected system in Burundi was recalculated as given in Annex 23.
The LRMC at the medium voltage level is estimated as BuF 12.1/kWh
(US010.3/kWh) and that at the low voltage (distribution) level is estimated
to be BuF 18.6/kWh (USt15.9/kWh).  The weighted average LRMC is estimated
at BuF 16.1/kWh (US13.8/kWh).  The projected tariffs adjustments (para.
5.13) would increase the average level to 80% of to the weighted average
LRMC by 1992. The differences in rates between consumer categories would
be reviewed during the implementation of the findings of the tariff study
(paras. 4.01 and 5.11) to ensure that they reflect correctly the
differences in supply costs.
Project Risks
6.14           The physical  risk  associated with  the  transmission  and
distribution components of this project is small because the work to be
completed is routine and only proven elements would be included. Risks of
higher costs due to receiving bids after presentation to the Board are also
small (para. 4.22).  The main risk would be institutional in nature, as
REGIDESO is generally weak in administration and management. However, this
risk would be minimized because (a) competent consultants would assist
REGIDESO in completing the project (para. 4.22), Cb) management assistance
team would be assisting REGIDESO in its day-to-day activities (para. 4.12),
and lc) the training component is expected to improve staff competency
particularly during the later stages of the project (para. 4.14). The risk
associated with the follow up,   in 1987 and 1988, of the dissemination
program of improved charcoal stoves in Bujumbura, is also small as
competent consultauts will continue to be employed to assist DUB (para.
4.15), and the first phase of the program in 1985 and 1986 will help to
minimize the risk for the follow-up phase.
VII.  AGREEMENTS REACHED AND RECOMNEINDATIONS
7.01       During negot Ltions, agreements were reached with the Government
and REGIDESO on the following:
(a) REGIDESO would arrange for prompt completion of the 1983 audit
and thereafter to have its accounts audited each year by an
independent auditor acceptable to IDA, and would submit audited
financial statements and auditor's reports to IDA no later than
six months after the end of the fiscal year (para. 3.07);



- 49 -
(b) REGIDESO would maintain separate accounts for its electricity
and water operations and would incorporate therein an annual
revaluation of its fixed assets in operation (para. 3.08);
(c) REGIDESO would apply a connections policy following consultation
with IDA, based on the recommendations of a study (para. 4.10);
(d) REGIDESO would retain the services of a management assistance
team by December 31, 1985 and implement during the life of the
project a progran of action satisfactory to IDA, based on the
conclusions of the management diagnosis (paras. 4.12 and 5.08);
(e) REGIDESO would prepare a detailed ten-year investment program,
for review with IDA, by June 30, 1986; and REGIDESO would update
the plan and eschange views with IDA annually (para. 4.13);
(f) REGIDESO would appoint a Manager of Training and three Burundese
trainers, and retain the services of three training specialists,
by October 1, 1985; these trainers would prepare and initiate a
training program acceptable to IDA, for the electricity and
related financial and administrative personnel of REGIDESO on or
before September 1, 1986 (para. 4.14);
(g) the Government would appoint by December 31, 1985 an expert to
provide advice on the purchase and sale of petroleum products
(para. 4.16);
'h) REGIDESO would continue to employ engineering consultants
acceptable to TDA (para. 4.22);
(i) REGIDESO would adjust its water tariffs to ensure that revenues
from water supply operations are at least sufficient to cover
operating expenses and debt service and provide a reasonable
contribution  to  the  water  supply  investment  program;  a
reasonable level of contribution would be agreed with IDA
(para. 5.01)
(i) REGIDESO would not incur debt unless internal cash generated for
the twelve months preceding incurrence of the debt is at least
1.5 times the maximam debt service requirement for any
succeeding year (para. 5.02).
(k) REGIDESO's outstanding receivable accounts for electricity and
water would not exceed: for Government and municipalities the
equivalent of six months billing at the end of 1986 and four
months billings at the end of 1987 and thereafter; and, for
other consumers, four months of billing at the end of 1985 and
four months billing for consumers billed every two months and
three months billing for consumers billed monthly at the end of
1986 and thereafter (para. 5.03);
(1) REGIDESO and the Government would implement a new tariff
structure consistent with the recomendations of the tariff
study, following consultation with IDA, and the new structure
would be fully effective by January 1, 1986 (para. 5.11);



-:~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~~~~s - D 
- 50 -
(m) REGIDESO and the Government would review the electricity tariff
structure annually with regard to' marginal COB t pricing
principles, cross-subsidization and extension of service to
lower income groups, and implement and approve tariffs so
developed which in total would produce revenues sufficient to
earn a rate of return on revalued net assets of not less than
4.0% in 1986 and 1987; 4.5% in 1988; 6.5Z in 1989, and 8% in
1990 and thereafter (paras. 5.11, 5.12 and 5.14);
(n) Government would agree to provide short-term funds as necessary
to ensure that REGIDESO has sufficient monies on an annual basis
to meet project construction costs, and REGIDESO would agree to
repay such funds within four years (para. 5.15); and
(o) REGIDESO would not commit itself, without prior consultation
with IDA, to any capital investment in excess of US$5 million
and would ensure that every investment in the electricity sector
would be economically and financially justified (para. 5.17).
7.02       Special conditions of effectiveness would be:
Ca) the agreement between IDA and REGIDESO on an action plan to
strengthen REGIDESO's manageaent (para. 4.12);
Cb) the agreement between IDA, the Government and REGIDESO on an
action plan to reduce Government's and municipalities' arrears
to six months of electricity and water billings by December 1986
(para. 5.03);
cc) the execution of the subsidiary loan agreement between the
Government of Burundi and REGIDESO (para. 5.05);
(d) the fulfillment of conditions precedent to disbursement of
cofinanciers' funde (para. 5.05); and,
(e) the agreement with Rwanda and Zaire that these countries
would provide a right-of-way and allow free access for the
construction, operation, and maintenance of the transmission
line from Ruzizi II to Bubanza (para. 4.06).
7.03           A condition of disbursement for the rehabilitation of the
Bujumbura substation would be that REGIDESO obtain legal rights adequate to
protect the interest of Burundi and IDA (paras. 4.07 and 4.24).
7.04        With the above agreements, the project is suitable for an IDA
Credit of SDR 12.9 million (USS12.3 million).
