BURUNDI
POWER TRANSMISSION AND DISTRIBUTION PROJECT
International Organizations
Coumunautg geouomiue des pas des grnds lacs (CEPGL)
1.        The Communautg economique des pays des grands lacs (CEPGL), is an
organization which was established in September 1976 by Burundi, Rwanda and
Zaire to revive the former cooperation among the three countries which
existed under the Belgian administration prior to independence. CEPGL was
formed to promote free movement of persons and goods within the area, and
to cooperate politically and economically within the region as it relates
to other countries in Africa.   The entity is made up of a council of
ministers, one from each of the countries, which meets twice a year and
reports to an annual meeting of the presidents of the three countries - the
highest authority of the organization. The day-to-day activities including
the preparation and execution of programs and coordination within the
administration of the three countries is handled by a Secretariat located
in Gisenyi, Rwanda. CEPGL receives assistance from USAID, France, Belgium
and FED for the preparation of feasibility studies.
2.           CEPGL bats sponsored a glass bottle manufacturing factory in
Burundi, and in June 1981, the International Finance Corporation (IFC)
approved a loan of USS4.0 million and an equity investment of US$0.75
million for its construction. The factory was placed in service in 1983.
Another activity is exploring the potential for the production of methane
from the deep waters of Lake Kivue    Several issues need to be resolved
before an investment program for gas development can be defined; for
example, the legal and institutional framework for gas extraction by Rwanda
and Zaire; the safety limitation and the establishment of the rate at which
the gas can be extracted; and the nature and the extent of the market and
the derivative products. The potential coutribution of the development of
gas to this area is still in the distant future.
Energie des pays des grands lacs (EGL)
3.         EGL was set up to ensure the availability of electric power in
the region, and as a result has promoted the construction of the Ruzizi It
hydroelectric power project on the Ruzizi River downstream from the
existing Ruzizi generating station on the border between Zaire and Rwanda
(Map LBRD 18517).   This organization, located in Bujumbura, Burundi, is
staffed with three technical directors - one each seconded from REGIDESO,
Burundi; ELECTROGAZ, Rwanda, and SNEL, Zaire; together with a small support
staff.
Kagera Basin Organization (KBO)
4.         This organization has its headquarters in Kigali, Rwanda, and as
in the case of EGL, is made up of a small staff seconded from each
country. At the request of KBO, several reports have been prepared on the



54
ANNEX 3
Page 2 of 2
development  of the Kagera River -  1967, Lahmeyer Internationsal  1976,
Norconsult and Electrowatt; 1979, Tractionel and Electrobel.
5.          Little action was taken ou the fiual report until 1981 when,
during meetings held by KB0 in Bujumbura in May, which were headed by the
Presidents of Burundi, Rwanda and Tanzania, a decision was made to proceed
with further study of the low-head i.e. a run-of-river scheme, at the
Rusumo Falls site on the Kagera River. However, a source of funds for the
study has not yet been found.   Because of its magnitude and cost, it is
likely that construction on this project may not begin until near the end
of the 1980s.  Nevertheless, Tanzania is interested in the development of
this project because, of the three countries, it has the least potential
for hydro generated power in this region.
SINELAC - The Regional Implementing Agency
6.          The three Governents of Burundi, Rwanda and Zaire in February
1984 ratified their agreement to form the international company, SINELAC,
to be the regional implementing agency of the Ruzizi II project.
7.         SINELAC, with its head office temporarily in Bujumbura, Burundi,
but to be moved to Bukavu, Zaire, by 1987, is an international public
company established for a 50-year renewable period, and the three
Governments of Burundi, Rwanda and Zaire contribute equally to its
capital.   Although SINELAC has been formed initially for the Ruzizi II
project, it could acquire and manage other electric power installations.
SINELAC is governed by the rules of the agreement and its own by-laws, and
for cases that are not covered by these rules and regulations by the
Investment Code of the Communautf &eonoaique des pays des grands lacs
(CEPGL), and by the laws of the country of its headquarters, Zaire.
SINELAC would operate as a commercial entity with financial objectives
defined initially in relation to the project and its electricity tariffs
would be established at a level which would produce a satisfactory rate of
return for the project.
8.        SINELAC is governed by a General Assembly consisting of the three
Mini3ters of Energy.   This General Assembly meets once a year and its
responsibilities are to appoint or dismiss the directors, the general
manager, the account controllers (coumissaires aux comptes) and the
auditors, and to discuss the financial statements of each previous year.
The Board of Directors consists of six members, two from each country. A
three member management committee is in charge of SINELAC's day-to-day
operations. SINELAC's General Manager is appointed by the General Assembly
and the Board of Directors has the responsibility of appointing and
removing the other two members of the management committee.   The three
members of the committee would be from different countries.   SINELAC
consults with IDA before appointing a new general manager.

BURUNDI
POWER TRANSMISSION AND DISTRIBUTION PROJECT
Summary Data on the Proposed Distribution Expansion
Bulumbura Districts
The number of new consumers to be connected in 1986 ard 1987 was
determined by consultants (EdY) based on their detailed study of the
districts based on past trends (including the districts of Ngagara and
Nyakabiga, medium and low-income districts already electrified), analysis
of household incomes. Consultants then determined the Installations to be
built within the proposed project and assessed REGIDESO's implementation
capacity. Cost estimates were based on recent prices and costs in Burundi
and in the region. REGIDESO would procure the equipment for connections to
be made in 1986 and 1987 and would make the connections; consumers would
pay half of the costs when the connection is made and would pay the other
half over twelve months in monthly installments. Cost of a connection is
estimated to be about BuF 60,000 (US$512). The penetration rate of
electrification by 1997 was assumed by IDA.

BURUNDI
POWER TRANSMISSION AND DISTRIBUTION PROJECT
Summary Data on the Proposed Subtransmission and Distribution Development
in Regional Towns
Cibitoke Town, Mparamnbo and Rugombo
Cibitoke town is situated 61 km northwest of Bujumbura.  There
are few small diesel generators totalling about 80 kVA. A coffee drying
factory with a load of about 550 kW will start operations by end-1985. A
550 KW diesel unit will be installed in the factory. A military camp, an
administrative center and 200-bed hospital, a mission, a mill a market
center, a school are other principal potential consumers. The first houses
to be electrified will be the lodgings of the Government employees. The
load was forecast to be about 750 kW; 1.6 GWh in 1988. Overall utilization
rate is low because of the low rate of the coffee factory.  In Rugombo,
which is situated north of the Cibitoke town, the potential consumers are a
market center, an administrative center and a large farm. In Mparambo, a
large farm with an existing 55 kW diesel unit is the largest potential
consumer.  Administrative and market centers are the other consumers.  For
the area it is estimated that the consumption would be 2.4 GUh in 1988 and
would Increase with an anmual growth rate of about 13.6% which is quite
reasonable compared to the potential of the area.
A 30 kV subtransmission line of about 21 km would go from
Cibitoke town to Rugombo via Mparambo.   Eignt 30/0.4 kV pole mounted
transformers of various capacities would be installed and about 4.0 km of
low voltage distribution lines would be constructed.  About 70 consumes,
commercial and domestic, would be connected in 1988.
Bubanza, Mpanda, Muzinda
Administrative, market and community centers, schools, cinemas,
post office, some workshops, garages, hospitals, missions, military camps,
and some small industries are the potential consumers in the is area north
of the capital. A mission operates a 60 kW diesel unit in Mpanda. It is
forecasted that the demand for electricity would be about 2.1 GWh in 1988;
the  growth  rate  is  expected  as  12%  per  annum.    21  km  of  30 kV
subtransoission line would be constructed from Bubanza to Mpanda and
Muzinda. Nine 30/0.4 kV pole mounted transformers of various capabilities
would be installed and 12.0 km of low voltage distribution lines would be
constructed. It is forecasted that in these localities, a total of about
290 consumers will be served by 1988.
Katumba
This small town situated next to the airport between Bujumbura
and the border with Zaire has virtually become a district of the capital.
Trade with Zaire is the main activity in the town and a large experimental
farm is located on the fields between the town and Lake Tanganyika.  The
customs post at the border will also be electrified. It is forecasted that



71
ANNEX 14
Page 2 of 2
the dernand for electricity would be 0.15 GWh in 1988 and that the growth
rate would be about 20X p.a. which is reasonable with respect to potential
commercial activity.   The 15 kV Bujumbura-Uvira (Zaire) line, owned and
operated hy S.N.EL. crosses the town but does not serve it.  S.N.EL. is
studying, within the proposed Zaire-Power II project (appraised in November
1984), the rehabilitation of the supply of Uvira and Kilimbe where a sugar
mill has been operating recently. This could include upgrading of the line
to 30 kV. Katumba would be supplied from the line by short feeder lines
with four 30 or 15/0.4 kV pole mounted transformers and about 4.0 km of
distribution lines.   It is expected that about 60 consuTers w-ould be
connected by 1988.

Proposed Program for Training Assistance to REGIDESO
1.        Summary of the Proposed Assistance
The proposed assistance would be closely coordinated with the GTZ
assistance (para. 4.14) and advantage would be taken of the qualifications
and experience of the advisers already in place.
2.        Proposed Program (agreed with REGIDESO during negotiations)

for the design of the training ceancer and the
preparation of bid documents for equipment; also
appointment of counterparts.

to                  trainees  and  definition  of  their  job  functions.
August 313 1986     Draft for study of course curricula and sequence based
on manpower projections for the next five years,
prepared  by  REGIDESO  personnel.    Finalization  of
trainee eligibility criteria. Issue of bid documents
and receipt of tenders and award of contracts for
equipment.
July 1, 1986        Installatlon  of  equipment  at  the  center  starts.
Finalization of course curricula.
September 1, 1986   Initiation of regular training program.
September, 1, 1987 Second training year.
September 1, 1988   Third  training  year  (Burundian  counterparts  assume
responsibility).
December 31, 1988   Experts depart.
3.        Draft Terms of Reference for 3 Trainers
The following is a brief list agreed during negotiations with
REGIDESO, of duties and activities which the training personnel are
expected to carry out during an assignment to REGIDESO in Burundi.   (A
description of the criteria for the expatriate and Burundian personnel is
in the project file.) Tasks are not necessarily in order of priority.

B. Administrative aad Financial Department
Skilled personnel and their supervisors
The level of instruction available through the national education
system means that REGIDESO can simply provide orientation directly in the
various divisions that make up this Department.
Newly recruited staff would require no more than an introduction
to the Corporation itself.
Professionals
It wo-uld be advisable to arrange for specific courses on the
cechaical procedures they are expected to follow. Most of them have only
their on-the-job experience, and  they  should be kept abreast of new
'evelopments that might affect their particular fields of responsibility.
Lthocse courses should be arranged for them at the proposed REGIDESO
training center.   Desirably internships should be organized in similar
organizations.
5.        Curriculum
If technical staff are to be competent to carry out operating
procedures (power stations or networks) or maintenance work on the circ;v'its
and actuators which make up the Corporation's facilities (power stations or
networks), they must pc3sess:
- the basic scientific knowledge required for an understanding of
the physical laws specific to a given trade or field of skill
(electrical, mecahnical, etc.);
- knowledge of the physical laws and related phenomena that enter
singly or simultaneously into the functioning of the circuits and
equipment on which they will be required to work (operating and
maintenauce procedures);



76
ANNEK 15
Page 5 of 6
- the know-how and skills specific to their function:
-  ability to analyze events or incidents that occur in the course
of operations and, if necessary, determine what action to take;
- familiarity with circuits and actuators:
- principle of operation;
- location in the installation;
- circuits that include or end in an actuator;
- procedures to be used, depending on the type of equipment or
circuit:
- tools required;
-- industrial safety measures to be taken;
- initiating technique;
- saquence of steps to be followed;
- evaluation of work carried out:
- tests and controls to use before resumption of service.
Depending  on actual employee  skill  levels  (known where new
recuits are concerned, to be ascertained in the case of existing staff),
formulation of the curricula sad course sequences to be adopted will
involve application of the pritciples set out above. There now follows, as
an example for other courses, an orientation course for operators due to be
assigned to jobs on the power distribution uetworks:

Proiect Monitoring
1.         Several factors affect the project implementation schedule and
the ultimate successful completion of the project. The key iteus to be
monitored would be as follows:
(a) Preparation and issue of bid docuAments June 30, 1985.
(b) Contract awards December 31, 1985.
(c) Construction progress.
(d) Testing and commissioning of the Ruzizi II-Bubanza 110 kV
transmission lines June 30, 1988.
(e) Progress on the technical assistance relative to the action
program agreed performance targets: variables to be uoaltored
will  be;  timetable  as  agreed  on  the  action  program
(para. 4.12); losses; number of connections per employer;
receivables in months of sales; operating ratio; internal cash
generation   contribution   to   construction   expenditures
(para. 4.26).
(f) Progress on the training activities with respect to the
program agreed at negotiations.
(g) Annual review of REGIDESO's financial status.
(h) Comparison of the actual performance relative to appraisal
forecast and financial covenants; variables to be monitored
will be: financial rate of return, debt service ratio,
accumulated cash, debt and debt plus equity ratio, currei.t
ratio, annual revaluation ratio.

BURUNDI
POWER TRANSMISSION AND DISTRIBUTION PROJECT
Notes on Financial Projections
Sales
1.         Sales for the period 1983-1991 were calculated on the basis of
the mission's demand estimates, which were sub-divided into domestic,
public agencies', commercial and industrial categories.   The resulting
average annual rates of growth are  11.4Z from 1983 to 1990 and 10%
thereafter.
Tariffs
2.         Average electricity tariffs have been calculated to produce an
increasing rate of return on rate base and an increasing internil cash
generatioa adequate to support financing for REGIDESO's investment
program.   Annual rate increases are projected at a level approximately
double the rate of internal inflation in the years 1985 tbrough 1987 and
50% greater than the estimated inflation until 1991.  For 1992 and 1993
rate increases are limited to 13% p.a.(para. 5.12).
Revenues
3.         Electricity revenues are developed from the sales estimates and
average tariffs as above. Other revenues are developed from present levels
adjusted for estimated new colnections.
Operating Expenses
4.         The cost of imported electricity has been calculated by taking
into consideration the price presently paid to S.N.EL. for the supply of
electricity from the Ruzizi I plant. Forecast prices were estimated on the
basis of calculations made in the Ruzizi II Project SAR.
5.         REGIDESO is presently overstaffed and an increase in number of
connections per employee is sought as a performnce target. This factor
has been taken into consideration in projecting the increase in the cost of
salaries at approximately 80% of the estimated inflation rate.
6.         The cost of materials, including costs applicable to expanded
service, is estimated to increase at approximately 16% p.a..
Depreciation
7.        Annmual rates of depreciation used by REGIDESO include:
Buildings 2.5%;
Generation facilities 5.0%;
Transmission and Distribution 4.0Z;
Vehicles 25%;
Office equipment, furniture and fittings 101



90
ANNEX 22
page 2 of 3
The resulting-composite rate, approximately 4.8%, is considered to be
higher than-appropriate for a system which is substantianly hydro-electric,
and a rate of 3.3Z has therefore been used in the projections.
Construction Expenditures
8.          The cost estimates for construction of the project components
have been estimated by REGIDESO's consultants, EdF (France), reviewed by
the mission and are considered reasonable. Costs for consulting services,
training, and for the management team and petroleum advisor, were prepareci
by the mission.  Details are given in paragraph 4.23.
Financing of the Project
9.         Terms of borrowing of the onlent IDA Credit are assumed to be a
repayment period of twenty years, including a five-year grace period and a
9.292 rate of interest. Current borrowings are at concessional financing
rates, with interest ranging from 2% to 5.5%.  Financing arranged for the
Rwegura project is also largely concessional, except for some 20Z of the
cost which is at 11.5% interest. For the project co-financing it has been
assumed that the repayment period will be twenty years including a five-
year grace period and an 8% rate of interest, reflecting the Government's
willingness to consider re-lending funds to REGIDESO at commercial rates;
as a first step the Governemnt would onlend to REGIDESO at the rate at
which the Government borrows plus 3 percent. REGIDESO's borrowing in the
past has beeen at an average interest rate of 5%.
Revaluation of Assets
10.       Assets are revalued with an average of international and domestic
i-ndices and incorporate Touche Ross' new evaluation for the 1980 assets.
Working Capital
11.         Accounts receivable are assumed to be in accordance with the
suggested covenant (para. 5.03). Accounts payable and Inventories increase
at approximately 11Z per annum, with cash balances being kept at a minimtm
level until repayment of the Government short-term advances. While large
cash surpluses are generated in 1991 and 1992, it is expected that these
will be used to .inance additional investments which would appear in the
least cost investment program to be finalized by June 30, 1986.
Long-Term Debt
11.          The sum of BuF 1,788 million is included as the amount out-
standing in respect of the Mugere project, financed by the People's Repu-
blic of China. Final disposition of this amount is yet to be determined as
between the Republic, the Government of Burundi and REGIDESO.   For the



91
ANNEX 22
page 3 of 3
purpose of the financial projections repayment has been assumed over a 20
year period commencing 1990. Tnterest at IOZ has been charged as-from this
date. Earlier payments are considered inappropriate in View of the excess
capacity which exists and the use of other than least-cost selections.
Government Funding
13.         Short-term financing is required in 1985 and 1986 and can be
repaid  over  the  1987-1990  period.    This: funding  is  treated  as
interest-free.   Previously, longer term financing has been supplied by
Government, described as tGrants,' and shown as Equity in the Balance
Sheet.

Economic Rate of Return Calculations for the Resionl Investunt Program
Assumptions: Project life 30 years
Demand forecasts: - Burundi (par&. 2.17); - Rwanda: SAR for Power
Project; - Zaire: latest estimte; giving for the region an anual
increase of 10X over the 1984-1995 period.
Sales of energy from Rwegura and Ruzim  II begin In 1988 and rech
US$224 GWh corresponding to full utilization of the facillties in
1995 (see page 5 of this annex).
1.  Calculation of Benefits
A. Without taking into account consumers' surplus:
Resulting sales in Burundi, Rwanda and Zaire (Kivu) multiplled by
the respective forecast retail tariffs,
B. Taking Into account consumers, surpluo:
The conosumers in the region whose consumption represents about
151 of the total demand from Ruizi II and Rwegura would be ready In
case the Rwegura and Ruzizi II projects were not built, to buy their
electrllty from a diesel-fueled generating statlon, at a cost of at
least US425/kWh. 1/ Either these consumers would have an urgent need
for electricity (Rospital, water pumping, Governoent agencles) or
their demand li very lnelastic (industries for which electricity is a
small part of their cost and which can pass the increase in
electricity cost to their customers, expatriates whose living expenses
are paid for, *tc)
Specific consumption of diesel oll:  0.3 kg/kWh.  Average economic
cost of diesel oil in the region: US450/llter 2/).
Remaining of the forecast sales from Rwegura and Ruzizi 11 assumed to
be paid through forecast electricity retail tariffs. The dea nd curve
for the region could be drawn with two points (1OOZ consumption at the
average tariff, and 15Z at diesel cost), and a conmsers' surplus
could be calculated that would increase the beneflts of the project.
1/ Staff Appraisal Report for the Ruzizi II Regional Hydroelectric Power
Project, May 1982; Report No. 4303-ZAP.
2/ Burundi-Review of Petroleum Import and Distribution Arrangement; ESHAP;
January 1984.

The revenue of the sale of Ruzlzi II and Rwegura electricity is
represented by the area abed, the value of which La TxQ. The
theoretical surplus of consumers ready to buy electricity up to the
diesel cost D is represented by the area above the tariff line limited
by the demand curve: ebcf. To simplify the calculation, we assume
that the fc curve is a straight llne, thus the value of the consumers'
surplus is: 0.15(D-T)Q + I 0.85(D-T)Q - 0.575(D-T)Q.
With construction expenditures C and revenues TQ and the above
consuierm' surplus, the economic rate of return is the discount rate at which
there Is equilibrium between C and TQ + 0.575(D-T)Q - (0.425T + 0.575D)Q.

ANNEX 25
Page I of 5
BURUNDI
POWER TRANSMISSION AND DISTRIBUTION PROJECT
Basis for Calculation of Economic Rate of Return
for the Subtransmission and Distribution Prolects in Cibitoke Town and
Bubanza areas and Katumba
1.         The economic rate of return was determined for each group; i.e.
Cibitoke town + Rugambo + Mparambo;  Bubanza + Mpanda + Muzinda  and
Katumba.  This rate is defined as the discount rate at which the present
values of all iacremental capital and operating costs and the benefits and
revenues attributable to the development, are equal.
Assumptions:
2.        Project life:  30 years
Costs are based on constant January 1985 prices.
Interest during construction and taxes not included.
Connection costs (BuF 60,000 (US$512) per connection) are paid by
consumers as consumers' contributions.
Sales of energy begin in 1988; number of consumers forecast by
REGIDESO and IDA as given in Annex 14.
Cost of energy is taken from Annex 23, para. 7; marginal cost of
energy from transmission to medium voltage: BuF 9.4/kWh. Losses
assumed to be 3.4%.
Electricity tariffs in constant prices assumed as given in
Annes 26.



108                         ANNEX 25
Page 2 of 5
Benefits:
Benefits were calculated with respect to electricity tariffs end also
considering consumers' surplus as follows:
Savings from existing diesel stations: amount generated in diesel units
estimated based on existing small diesel units 1/; no new units assumed
to be installed; specific consumption: 0.4kg/kWh; economic cost (border
price plus transportation cost in Burundi) of diesel oil: BuF 67/1; 2/
no increase on the cost of diesel oil was considered to keep the
economic justification on the conservative side; remaining of the fore-
cast sales assumed to be paid through electricity tariffs (for Katumba:
10% of the sales assumed to substitute very small diesel units).
Computation
3.      The streams of costs and revenues are shown in the following pages.
Sensitivity Studies
4.        Sensitivity studies were carried out assuming a cost increase of
10% and an increase in the demand in these areas of 8.5% p.a. resulting in
a delay of about one year in benefits.   Results are summarized in the
following table:
Summary of the ERR Calculations for the MV and Distribution Developments at
Cibitoke Town and Bubanza Areas and Katumba
(Z)
Consumers' Surplus Considered
All              Costs   Benefits
Benefits by   Base     up    Late by

Cibitoke town + Rugombo +
Mparando                          11.4       17.1    15.9     15.3      14.2
Bubanza + Mpanda + Muzinda         10.3      11.4    10.6      10.5      9.8
Katumba                             8.5      10.8    10.0       9.9       9.2
1/ Cibitoke town + Rugombo + Mparambo:
- military camp: 25 kVA; mission :15 kVA; flour mill: 32 kW; total: 64 kW;
utilization 4,000 hly; energy to be generated: 0.256 GWhly.
- tobacco drying factory: 550 kW; utilization: 1,200 h/y; energy to be
generated :0.660 GWh/y.
- total: 0.916 GWhJy.
- Bubanza + Mpanda + Muzinda:
- Mpanda: 60 kW; utilization:4,000 h/y; energy to be generated: 0.240
GWhly.
- various missions.: 50 kW; utilization: 2,000 hly; energy to be generated;
0.100 GWh/y.
- total: 0.340 GWhJ/y
- Katumba: none.
2/ Burundi - Review of petroleum import and distribution arrangements -
ESKAP; January 1984.

112                         ANNEX 26
Page 1 of 9
BURDiNDI
POWER TRANSMISSION AND DISTRIBUTION PROJECT
Basis for Calculation of Economic Rate of Return
for the Distribution Expansion In Bujumbura Districts
1.         The economic rate of return for the distribution extensions was
determined for each district. This rate is defined as the discount rate at
which the present values of all incremental capital and operating costs,
and the benefits and revenues attributable to the development, are equal.
Assumtions:
2.        Project life:  30 years
Costs are based on constant January 1985 prices.
Interest during construction and taxes not included.
Connection costs (BuF 60,000 (US$512) per cnnnection) paid by
consumers as consumers' contribution.
Sales of energy begin in 1987 to consumers connected In 1986.
Number of consumers to be comnected In 1986 and 1987 determined
by EdF based on detailed study of each district and REGIDKSO's
manpower capacity for the construction of the networks.
Assumption on the penetration of electrification of housebolds In
20 years by IDA in Annes 13.
EdP sales forecast: 2,000 kWh/year per consumer: Main criteria:
(i) it is assumed that 100 kWh/year It per consumer will be used
to substitute the kerosene wick lamps; 2/ (ii) lOX of the demand
would substitute for generation from very small diesel units to
be used In service stations, garages, small workshops; and,
(lii) the rest is assumed to be pald through electricity tariffs.
Sensitivity studies carried out with 1,800, 1,500 and 1,000
kWh/year per consumer.
Benefits from substitution of wick lamps:
- cost of wick lamps: US$7.5
- life: 3 years
- cost of wick: US$0.40
- maintenance: 4 wicks per year
- each household uses 3 lamps
- each lamp is used 3 hours per day
- specific consumption: 0.012 liter/h
- economic cost of kerosene:  BuF 67Jliter (border price plus
transportation costs in Burundi; no Increase on the cost of
kerosene was considered to keep the economic justiflcation on
the conservative side).

The economic rate of return, excluding consumers' surplus was calculated
for the base case (with 2,000 kWh/a per consumer) as 6.0. This rate shows
that the electricity tariffs are not sufficient to provide a good rate of
return for this part of the project; however the savings In liported diesel
oil and kerosene are large enough and the economic rates of return for the
whole of the economy are acceptable.
